   <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style>

      <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Basic_forms_of_government" title="Template:Basic forms of government"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>

<p>This is a list of <a href="/wiki/Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Countries">countries</a> by <a href="/wiki/System_of_government" class="mw-redirect" title="System of government">system of government</a>. There is also a <a href="/wiki/Map" title="Map">political mapping</a> of the world that shows what form of government each country has, as well as a brief description of what each form of government entails. The list is colour-coded according to the type of government, for example: blue represents a republic with an executive <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, and pink is a constitutional monarchy with a <a href="/wiki/Figurehead" title="Figurehead">ceremonial head of state</a>. The colour-coding also appears on the following map, representing the same government categories. The <a href="#Legend">legend</a> of what the different colours represent is found just below the map. </p>
<p>It is noteworthy that some scholars in <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> claim that the country's system of <a href="/wiki/Government_of_China" title="Government of China">government</a> is a "Semi-presidential system combining party and government in actual operation".<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Under <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Constitution of the People's Republic of China">China's constitution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="President of the People's Republic of China">Chinese President</a> is a largely <a href="/wiki/Figurehead" title="Figurehead">ceremonial office</a> with limited power.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> However, since 1993, as a matter of convention, the presidency has been held simultaneously by the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party" title="General Secretary of the Chinese Communist Party">General Secretary of the Communist Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Paramount_leader" title="Paramount leader">top leader</a> in the <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party system</a> who heads the <a href="/wiki/Politburo_Standing_Committee_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Politburo Standing Committee of the Chinese Communist Party">Politburo Standing Committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Head_of_China_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Head_of_China-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_countries">List of countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: List of countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Map">Map</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Map">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<div class="center">
 <div class="floatnone">
  <a href="/wiki/File:Forms_of_government.svg" class="image" title="A colour-coded legend of forms of government."><img alt="A colour-coded legend of forms of government." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Forms_of_government.svg/1000px-Forms_of_government.svg.png" decoding="async" width="1000" height="512" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Forms_of_government.svg/1500px-Forms_of_government.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Forms_of_government.svg/2000px-Forms_of_government.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="921" data-file-height="472"></a>
 </div>
</div> 
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legend">Legend</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Legend">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<ul>
 <li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#3054dE; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>Presidential republic:</b> Head of state is also head of government and is independent of legislature
  </div></li> 
 <li>
  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#F0E945; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>Semi-presidential republic:</b> Head of state has some executive powers and is independent of legislature; remaining executive power is vested in ministry that is subject to parliamentary confidence
  </div></li> 
 <li>
  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#66BC66; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>Republic with an executive presidency nominated by or elected by the legislature:</b> President is both head of state and government; ministry, including the president, may or may not be subject to parliamentary confidence
  </div></li> 
 <li>
  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FF9B30; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>Parliamentary republic with a ceremonial presidency:</b> Head of state is ceremonial; ministry is subject to parliamentary confidence
  </div></li> 
 <li>
  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#EF13F9; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>Constitutional monarchy:</b> Head of state is executive; Monarch personally exercises power in concert with other institutions
  </div></li> 
 <li>
  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#E85252; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>Constitutional parliamentary monarchy:</b> Head of state is ceremonial; ministry is subject to parliamentary confidence
  </div></li> 
 <li>
  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#811381; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>Absolute monarchy:</b> Head of state is executive; all authority vested in absolute monarch
  </div></li> 
 <li>
  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#AC7030; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<b>One-party state:</b> Head of state is executive or ceremonial; power constitutionally linked to a single political movement
  </div></li> 
 <li>
  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
  <div class="legend">
   <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#818181; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<i><b>No constitutionally defined basis to current regime</b></i>
  </div></li>
</ul> 
<p>Note: this chart represent <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i><span class="lang-comment" style="font-style: normal; display: none; color: #33aa33; margin-left: 0.3em;">code: lat promoted to code: la </span> systems of government, not the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i><span class="lang-comment" style="font-style: normal; display: none; color: #33aa33; margin-left: 0.3em;">code: lat promoted to code: la </span> degree of democracy. Several states that are constitutional republics are in practice ruled as authoritarian states. </p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems_of_governance">Systems of governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Systems of governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
<p><i>Italics</i> indicate states with limited recognition. </p> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidential_systems">Presidential systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Presidential systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>These are systems in which a <a href="/wiki/President_(government_title)" title="President (government title)">president</a> is the active head of the <a href="/wiki/Executive_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive branch">executive branch</a> of government, and is elected and remains in office independently of the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a>. </p>
<p>In full <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential systems</a>, the president is both head of state and head of government. There is generally no prime minister, although if one exists, in most cases, he or she serves purely at the discretion of the president (with the exceptions being Belarus and Kazakhstan, where the prime minister is effectively the head of government).<sup id="cite_ref-BL_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BL-5">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KZ_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KZ-6">[5]</a></sup> </p>
<p>The following list includes democratic and non-democratic states: </p> 
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidential_systems_without_a_prime_minister">Presidential systems without a prime minister</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Presidential systems without a prime minister">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Semi-presidential_systems">Semi-presidential systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Semi-presidential systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential systems</a>, there is always both a president and a head of government, commonly but not exclusively styled <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">Prime Minister</a>. In such systems, the president has genuine executive authority, unlike in a parliamentary republic, but the role of a head of government may be exercised by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a>. </p> 
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Premier-presidential_systems">Premier-presidential systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Premier-presidential systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p> The president chooses the prime minister and cabinet, but only the parliament may remove them from office with a <i>vote of no confidence</i>. The president does <i>not</i> have the right to dismiss the prime minister or the cabinet.
 <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716"></p>
<div class="div-col"> 
 <ul>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="President-parliamentary_systems">President-parliamentary systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: President-parliamentary systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<p>The president chooses the prime minister and the cabinet without the <a href="/wiki/Confidence_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Confidence vote">confidence vote</a> from the parliament, but must have the support of the parliament majority for their choice. In order to remove a prime minister or the whole cabinet from power, the president can dismiss them or the assembly can remove them by a <i>vote of no confidence</i>. </p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_and_related_systems">Parliamentary and related systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Parliamentary and related systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>, the head of government is selected by, or nominated by, the legislature and is also accountable to it. The head of state is ordinarily called president, and in most parliamentary republics is separate from the head of government and serves as a largely apolitical, ceremonial figure. In these systems, the head of government is usually called prime minister, chancellor or premier. In mixed republican systems and directorial republican systems, the head of government also serves as head of state and is usually titled president. </p> 
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Full_parliamentary_republican_systems">Full parliamentary republican systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Full parliamentary republican systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<p>In some full parliamentary systems, the head of state is directly elected by voters. Under some classification systems, however, these systems may instead be classed as semi-presidential systems, despite their weak presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[7]</a></sup> Full parliamentary systems that do not have a directly elected head of state usually use either an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_college" title="Electoral college">electoral college</a> or a vote in the legislature to appoint the head of state. </p>

<p>Nations with limited recognition are in italics. </p> 
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliamentary_republics_with_an_executive_presidency">Parliamentary republics with an executive presidency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Parliamentary republics with an executive presidency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<p>A combined head of state and government in the form of an <a href="/wiki/Executive_president" title="Executive president">executive president</a> is either elected by the legislature or by the voters after a few candidates are nominated for the post by the legislature (in the case of <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>), and they must maintain the confidence of the legislature to remain in office. </p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Assembly-independent_republican_systems">Assembly-independent republican systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Assembly-independent republican systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<p>A combined head of state and head of government (usually titled "president") is elected by the legislature but is immune from a vote of no confidence (as is their cabinet), unlike a prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[27]</a></sup> They may or may not hold a seat in the legislature. </p> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
<div class="div-col"> 
 <ul>
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Flag_of_the_Federated_States_of_Micronesia.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Federated_States_of_Micronesia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Flag_of_the_Federated_States_of_Micronesia.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Federated_States_of_Micronesia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Flag_of_the_Federated_States_of_Micronesia.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Federated_States_of_Micronesia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="400">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a><sup id="cite_ref-Combo_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Combo-34">[note 7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[28]</a></sup></li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Directorial_republican_systems">Directorial republican systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Directorial republican systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Directorial_system" title="Directorial system">directorial system</a>, a council jointly exercises the powers of both head of state and head of government. The council is elected by the parliament, but it is not subject to <a href="/wiki/Confidence_(political_science)" class="mw-redirect" title="Confidence (political science)">parliamentary confidence</a> during its term which has a fixed duration. </p> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
<div class="div-col"> 
 <ul>
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/16px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/24px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a><sup id="cite_ref-CH_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CH-39">[note 10]</a></sup></li>
 </ul> 
</div> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_monarchies">Constitutional monarchies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Constitutional monarchies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>These are systems in which the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional monarch">constitutional monarch</a>; the existence of their office and their ability to exercise their authority is established and restrained or held back by constitutional law. </p> 
<h4><span id="Constitutional_monarchies_with_ceremonial.2Fnon-executive_monarchs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_monarchies_with_ceremonial/non-executive_monarchs">Constitutional monarchies with ceremonial/non-executive monarchs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Constitutional monarchies with ceremonial/non-executive monarchs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<p>Systems in which a <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> is the active head of the <a href="/wiki/Executive_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive branch">executive branch</a> of government. In some cases the prime minister is also leader of the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a>, in other cases the executive branch is clearly separated from legislature although the entire cabinet or individual ministers must step down in the case of a <a href="/wiki/Vote_of_no_confidence" class="mw-redirect" title="Vote of no confidence">vote of no confidence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[31]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (November 2008)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:List_of_countries_by_system_of_government#Constitutional_monarchy" title="Talk:List of countries by system of government">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarch" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional monarch">constitutional monarch</a> who normally only exercises his or her powers (some monarchs are given a limited number of discretionary 'reserve' powers, only to be used in certain circumstances; many monarchs are given the responsibility to defend the nation's constitution) with the consent of the government, the people and/or their representatives (except in emergencies, e.g. a constitutional crisis or a political deadlock). </p> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
<div class="div-col"> 
 <ul>
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/22px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png" decoding="async" width="22" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/33px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Flag_of_Andorra.svg/43px-Flag_of_Andorra.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="700">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a><sup id="cite_ref-and_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-and-42">[note 11]</a></sup></li>

<p>Note: Andorra may be considered a theocracy as the monarch is a joint head of state, one of whom is a religious figure.<sup id="cite_ref-and_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-and-42">[note 11]</a></sup> </p> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_monarchies_with_active_monarchs">Constitutional monarchies with active monarchs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Constitutional monarchies with active monarchs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>The prime minister is the nation's active executive, but the monarch still has considerable political powers that can be used at their own discretion. </p> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">

  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Bahrain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bahrain.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Bahrain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bahrain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Bahrain.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bahrain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="900">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Absolute_monarchies">Absolute monarchies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Absolute monarchies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>Specifically, monarchies in which the monarch's exercise of power is unconstrained by any substantive constitutional law. </p> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_absolute_monarchies">Traditional absolute monarchies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Traditional absolute monarchies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
<div class="div-col"> 
 <ul>
  <li class="mw-empty-elt"></li> 
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Brunei.svg/23px-Flag_of_Brunei.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Brunei.svg/35px-Flag_of_Brunei.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Brunei.svg/46px-Flag_of_Brunei.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="720">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a></li> 
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a></li> 
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/16px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="16" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/24px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a><sup id="cite_ref-Va_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Va-48">[note 14]</a></sup></li>
 </ul> 
</div> 
<p>Notes: Vatican City may be considered a theocracy as the monarch is elected by a religious body,<sup id="cite_ref-Va_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Va-48">[note 14]</a></sup> </p> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Absolute_monarchies_with_democratically_elected_legislature">Absolute monarchies with democratically elected legislature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Absolute monarchies with democratically elected legislature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<ul>
 <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Flag_of_Eswatini.svg/23px-Flag_of_Eswatini.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Flag_of_Eswatini.svg/35px-Flag_of_Eswatini.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Flag_of_Eswatini.svg/45px-Flag_of_Eswatini.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[36]</a></sup></li> 
 <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Oman.svg/23px-Flag_of_Oman.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Oman.svg/35px-Flag_of_Oman.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_Oman.svg/46px-Flag_of_Oman.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[37]</a></sup></li>
</ul> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="One-party_states">One-party states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: One-party states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>States in which political power is <i>by law</i> concentrated within <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one political party</a> whose operations are largely fused with the government hierarchy (as opposed to states where the law establishes a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a> but <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">this fusion is achieved anyway through electoral fraud or simple inertia</a>). However, some do have elected governments. </p> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
<div class="div-col"> 
 <ul>
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China, People's Republic of</a> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party of China">Communist Party</a> leads the <a href="/wiki/United_Front_(People%27s_Republic_of_China)" class="mw-redirect" title="United Front (People's Republic of China)">United Front</a>) (<a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="List of political parties in the People's Republic of China">list</a>)</small></li> 
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Flag_of_Cuba.svg/46px-Flag_of_Cuba.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Cuba" title="Communist Party of Cuba">Communist Party</a>) (<a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Cuba" title="List of political parties in Cuba">list</a>)</small></li> 
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Flag_of_Eritrea.svg/23px-Flag_of_Eritrea.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Flag_of_Eritrea.svg/35px-Flag_of_Eritrea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Flag_of_Eritrea.svg/46px-Flag_of_Eritrea.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> <small>(<a href="/wiki/People%27s_Front_for_Democracy_and_Justice" title="People's Front for Democracy and Justice">People's Front for Democracy and Justice</a>) (<a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Eritrea" title="List of political parties in Eritrea">list</a>)</small></li> 
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Flag_of_North_Korea.svg/23px-Flag_of_North_Korea.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Flag_of_North_Korea.svg/35px-Flag_of_North_Korea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Flag_of_North_Korea.svg/46px-Flag_of_North_Korea.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="800">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">Korea, North</a> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Korea" title="Workers' Party of Korea">Workers' Party</a> leads the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Front_for_the_Reunification_of_the_Fatherland" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Front for the Reunification of the Fatherland">Democratic Front</a>) (<a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_North_Korea" title="List of political parties in North Korea">list</a>)</small></li> 
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Laos.svg/23px-Flag_of_Laos.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Laos.svg/35px-Flag_of_Laos.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Laos.svg/45px-Flag_of_Laos.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Lao_People%27s_Revolutionary_Party" title="Lao People's Revolutionary Party">People's Revolutionary Party</a> leads the <a href="/wiki/Lao_Front_for_National_Construction" title="Lao Front for National Construction">Front for National Construction</a>) (<a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Laos" title="List of political parties in Laos">list</a>)</small></li>

  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/23px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/35px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Flag_of_Vietnam.svg/45px-Flag_of_Vietnam.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Vietnam" title="Communist Party of Vietnam">Communist Party</a> leads the <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Fatherland_Front" title="Vietnamese Fatherland Front">Fatherland Front</a>) (<a href="/wiki/List_of_Vietnamese_political_parties" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Vietnamese political parties">list</a>)</small></li>
 </ul> 
</div> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_dictatorships">Military dictatorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Military dictatorships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>The nation's military control the organs of government and all high-ranking political executives are also members of the military hierarchy. </p> 
<ul>
 <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Mali.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mali.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Mali.svg/35px-Flag_of_Mali.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Mali.svg/45px-Flag_of_Mali.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(<a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-presidential republic">semi-presidential republic</a>)</span></li>
</ul> 
<p>Many other states have been run by military governments in the past such as <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> under the <a href="/wiki/State_Peace_and_Development_Council" title="State Peace and Development Council">State Peace and Development Council</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> was governed by a <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship_of_Chile_(1973%E2%80%931990)" title="Military dictatorship of Chile (1973–1990)">military dictatorship</a> for 17 years between 1973 and 1990. <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> was also governed by a <a href="/wiki/Martial_law_in_Taiwan" title="Martial law in Taiwan">military dictatorship</a> from 1949 to 1987. </p> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
<div class="div-col"> 
</div> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transitional_governments">Transitional governments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transitional governments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<p>States that have a system of government that is in transition or turmoil and are classified with the current direction of change. </p> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">
<div class="div-col"> 
 <ul>
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Libya.svg/23px-Flag_of_Libya.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Libya.svg/35px-Flag_of_Libya.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Libya.svg/46px-Flag_of_Libya.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="480">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(<a href="/wiki/Provisional_government" title="Provisional government">provisional government</a>)</span></li> 
  <li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Flag_of_Sudan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sudan.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Flag_of_Sudan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sudan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Flag_of_Sudan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sudan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600">&nbsp;</span><a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(<a href="/wiki/Provisional_government" title="Provisional government">provisional government</a>)</span></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems_of_internal_structure">Systems of internal structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Systems of internal structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unitary_states">Unitary states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Unitary states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
 Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">Unitary state</a>
</div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> governed as a single power in which the <a href="/wiki/Central_government" title="Central government">central government</a> is ultimately supreme and any <a href="/wiki/Administrative_division" title="Administrative division">administrative divisions</a> (sub-national units) exercise only the powers that the central government chooses to delegate. </p>
<p>The majority of states in the world have a unitary system of government. Of the 193 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">UN member states</a>, 165 are governed as unitary states. </p> 
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Centralised_unitary_states">Centralised unitary states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Centralised unitary states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<p>States in which most power is exercised by the central government. What local authorities do exist have few powers. </p> 
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Regionalised_unitary_states">Regionalised unitary states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Regionalised unitary states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
 Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regional_state" title="Regional state">Regional state</a>
</div> 
<p>States in which the <a href="/wiki/Central_government" title="Central government">central government</a> has delegated some of its powers to regional authorities, but where constitutional authority ultimately remains entirely at a national level. </p> 
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federation">Federation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Federation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
 Main article: <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">Federation</a>
</div> 
<p>States in which the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal government">federal government</a> shares power with regional governments with which it has legal or constitutional <a href="/wiki/Parity" class="mw-disambig" title="Parity">parity</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Disambiguation/Fixing_links" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Disambiguation/Fixing links"><span title="Link needs disambiguation (December 2020)">disambiguation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The central government may or may not be (in theory) a creation of the regional governments. </p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
 Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_Union_member_states_by_political_system" title="List of European Union member states by political system">List of European Union member states by political system</a>
</div> 
<p>The exact political character of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> is debated, some arguing that it is <i lang="la" title="Latin language text"><a href="/wiki/Sui_generis" title="Sui generis">sui generis</a></i><span class="lang-comment" style="font-style: normal; display: none; color: #33aa33; margin-left: 0.3em;">code: lat promoted to code: la </span> (unique), but others arguing that it has features of a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a>. It has elements of <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmentalism" title="Intergovernmentalism">intergovernmentalism</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> acting as its collective "president", and also elements of <a href="/wiki/Supranationalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Supranationalism">supranationalism</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> acting as its executive and bureaucracy.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[38]</a></sup> But it is not easily placed in any of the above categories.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_system_of_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
 <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
  <ol class="references"> 
   <li id="cite_note-CHNhead-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-CHNhead_4-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="President of the People's Republic of China">President of China</a> is legally a <a href="/wiki/Figurehead" title="Figurehead">ceremonial office</a> without considering the presidency held simultaneously by the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party" title="General Secretary of the Chinese Communist Party">General Secretary of the Chinese Communist Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Head_of_China_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Head_of_China-3">[3]</a></sup></span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-Ir-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Ir_7-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Iran combines the forms of a presidential republic, with a president elected by universal suffrage; and a theocracy, with a <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Leader_of_Iran" title="Supreme Leader of Iran">Supreme Leader</a> who is ultimately responsible for state policy, chosen by the elected <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Experts" title="Assembly of Experts">Assembly of Experts</a>. Candidates for both the Assembly of Experts and the presidency are vetted by the appointed <a href="/wiki/Guardian_Council" title="Guardian Council">Guardian Council</a>.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Collective presidency consisting of three members; one for each major ethnic group.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Formerly a semi-presidential republic, it is now a parliamentary republic according to David Arter, First Chair of Politics at Aberdeen University, who in his "Scandinavian Politics Today,"<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[12]</a></sup> he quotes<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup> as follows: "There are hardly any grounds for the epithet 'semi-presidential'." Arter's own conclusions are only slightly more nuanced: "The adoption of a new constitution on 1 March 2000 meant that Finland was no longer a case of semi-presidential government other than in the minimalist sense of a situation where a popularly elected fixed-term president exists alongside a prime minister and cabinet who are responsible to parliament (Elgie 2004: 317)". According to the Finnish Constitution, the President has no possibility to rule the government without the ministerial approval, and substantially has not the power to disband the parliament under its own desire. Finland is actually represented by its Prime Minister, and not by its President, in the Council of the Heads of State and Government of the European Union. The 2012 constitutional amendments reduced the powers of the President even further.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-Bd-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Bd_27-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In Bangladesh, a <a href="/wiki/Caretaker_government_of_Bangladesh" title="Caretaker government of Bangladesh">caretaker government</a> was in power during parliamentary elections. The Caretaker Government was headed by a Chief Adviser and a group of neutral, non-partisan advisers chosen from the civil society. During this time, the president had jurisdiction over the defence and foreign affairs ministries. But according to the 15th amendment of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bangladesh" title="Constitution of Bangladesh">Constitution of Bangladesh</a> , the provisions of Caretaker Government is abolished.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-28">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The president is elected by parliament and holds a parliamentary seat, much like a prime minister, but is immune from a vote of no confidence (but not their cabinet), unlike a prime minister. Although, if a vote of no confidence is successful and they do not resign, it triggers the dissolution of the legislature and new elections (per section 92 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Botswana" title="Constitution of Botswana">Constitution</a>).</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-Combo-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Combo_34-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Holds a parliamentary seat.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-Assembly-independent-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Assembly-independent_36-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Assembly-independent_36-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Does not hold a parliamentary seat.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-37">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Their two-person head of state and head of government, the <a href="/wiki/Captains_Regent" title="Captains Regent">Captains Regent</a>, serve for six month terms, although they are not subject to parliamentary confidence during that time.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-CH-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-CH_39-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Swiss_Confederation" title="President of the Swiss Confederation">President of Switzerland</a> serves in a <i><a href="/wiki/Primus_inter_pares" title="Primus inter pares">primus inter pares</a></i> capacity amongst the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Federal Council">Swiss Federal Council</a>, the seven-member executive council which constitutes both the presidency and the government.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-and-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-and_42-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-and_42-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Urgell">Bishop of Urgell</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President of France</a> serve as <i><a href="/wiki/Ex_officio" class="mw-redirect" title="Ex officio">ex officio</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Co-Prince_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-Prince of Andorra">co-princes</a> who have their interests known through a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor-General">representative</a>.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-Commonwealthrealm-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-14"><sup><i><b>o</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-15"><sup><i><b>p</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-16"><sup><i><b>q</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Commonwealthrealm_43-17"><sup><i><b>r</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">One of sixteen constitutional monarchies which recognize <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Elizabeth II</a> as head of state, who presides over an independent government. She is titled separately in each country (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Australia">Queen of Australia</a>), and notionally appoints a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor-General">Governor-General</a> (GG) to each country other than the United Kingdom to act as her representative. The <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> (PM) is the active head of the executive branch of government and also leader of the legislature. These countries may be known as "<a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>".<br>In many cases, the Governor-General or monarch has a lot more theoretical, or constitutional, powers than they actually exercise, except on the advice of elected officials, per <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_convention_(political_custom)" title="Constitutional convention (political custom)">constitutional convention</a>. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Australia" title="Constitution of Australia">Constitution of Australia</a> makes the GG the head of the executive branch (including <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the armed forces), although they seldom ever use this power, except on the advice of elected officials, especially the PM, which makes the PM the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> head of government.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-NZ-Monarch-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-NZ-Monarch_44-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NZ-Monarch_44-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NZ-Monarch_44-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a> are under the sovereignty of the Monarch of New Zealand as self-governing <a href="/wiki/Associated_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Associated states">states in free association</a> with New Zealand. New Zealand and its associated states, along with <a href="/wiki/Tokelau" title="Tokelau">Tokelau</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ross_Dependency" title="Ross Dependency">Ross Dependency</a>, comprise the <a href="/wiki/Realm_of_New_Zealand" title="Realm of New Zealand">Realm of New Zealand</a>.</span> </li> 
   <li id="cite_note-Va-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Va_48-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Va_48-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The Vatican is an <a href="/wiki/Elective_monarchy" title="Elective monarchy">elective</a> absolute monarchy and a Roman Catholic theocracy; its monarch, the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a>, is the head of the global <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>. His power within the Vatican City State is unlimited by any constitution; however, as all its citizens and its residents are ordained Catholic clergy, members of the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Guard" title="Swiss Guard">Swiss Guard</a>, or their immediate family, they arguably have consented to obey the Pope or are minors. (Citizenship is <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">jus officii</i><span class="lang-comment" style="font-style: normal; display: none; color: #33aa33; margin-left: 0.3em;">code: lat promoted to code: la </span>, on the grounds of appointment to work in a certain capacity in the service of the Holy See and usually ceases upon cessation of the appointment. Citizenship is also extended to the spouse and children of a citizen, provided they are living together in the city. Some individuals are also authorized to reside in the city but do not qualify or choose not to request citizenship.)<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[34]</a></sup></span> </li> 
  </ol>
 </div>
</div>

   <li id="cite_note-Head_of_China-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Head_of_China_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Head_of_China_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">

     <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFAbdurasulov2017" class="citation news cs1">Abdurasulov, Abdujalil (6 March 2017). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-39177708">"Kazakhstan constitution: Will changes bring democracy?"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
